Preface 
This master thesis project is done in the period of 15th of September 2014 to 1st of March 
2015. This 32.5 ECTS points project is final part of master program at Petroleum 
engineering in Technical University of Denmark (DTU). 
The result of this project is mainly achieved based on the experimental works, which are 
performed on Stevns chalk. In addition, results are compared to results in available 
literatures.

Abstract 
To investigate strength criteria from rock mechanics, samples from Stevns Klint are 
exploited. In this project, the strength of Stevns chalk by performing Brazilian test, UCS test, 
Triaixal compressive test and triaxial extension test is evaluated. Chalk samples in this 
study have an average porosity of 44.10% with 2.7𝑔/𝑐𝑐  grain density. 
Besides evaluating the strength of chalk full isotropy of samples are also studied.  
Tensile strength demonstrated isotropic behavior. For all three directions tensile strength 
was equal to 0.3 𝑀𝑃𝑎. Based on experimental evaluation compressive strengths 
were 1.69 𝑀𝑃𝑎, 1.37 𝑀𝑝𝑎 and 1.21 𝑀𝑃𝑎 
for 
vertical, 
Horizontal1 
and 
Horizontal2 
directions. Therefore, samples show anisotropic behavior for compressive strengths .Bulk 
moduli and Tangent Young’s moduli also represent anisotropic behavior based on the 
achieved experimental results from UCS, Triaxial compressive and Triaxial extension Tests. 
Evaluation of failure line based on the p-q diagram and Mohr-coulomb plot represents that 
cohesion and friction angle values are higher in compressive tests than extension tests. 
Cohesions and friction angle values for compressive and extension tests are reported in the 
following table:

1-Introduction 
Many studies are done for mechanical behavior of porous chalk .This studies is practiced in 
order to understand the application of rock mechanics in borehole stability, compaction 
and solid production. Earlier work focused on estimating strength of chalk. Studies are 
done on chalk because chalk is an important rock in the southern part of North Sea (R.I. 
Korsnes, 2008) moreover approximately 50% of the petroleum reservoirs in the world are 
explored in carbonates formation (limestone, chalk and dolomite) (B. Zangiabadi, 2009). 
Chalks are naturally very soft and contain more oil in place because of high porosity (David 
E. Simon, 1982). 
Experimental studies evaluated strength, study failure behavior of chalk by Mohr-Coulomb 
criteria, calculated cohesion and friction angle based on 𝑝−𝑞 diagram and Mohr-Coulomb 
criteria. These evaluations are done by conducting Brazilian, Uniaxial strength and 
compressive Triaxial test in ambient and high temperature. (Merete Vadla Madland, 2002) 
(G. Wiseman, 1966).  Some other papers presented the results from running series of 
Triaxial extension test and used data of Brazilian, UCS and compressive Triaxial test from 
the others laboratory experience (Rasmus Risnes, 1996). 
Sound measurement is recorded in many studied for different purposes, Cote et al. 
evaluated rock failure process during Brazilian test by recording sound waves (H.COTE, 
1999), Olsen et al. assessed elastic properties of chalk and finally Fabricius et al. checked 
the effect of burial depth on porosity and sonic velocity (Ida L. Fabricius, 2008) 
furthermore they measured elastic moduli of North Sea chalk based on the undrained test 
results. (Ida L. Fabricius, 2010). 
The effect of anisotropy on strength of chalk it has been documented by testing samples in 
various directions. Korsnes et al. shows the mechanical properties of Liege and Stevns 
displayed anisotropic behavior, expect permeability (Liege Chalk) and tensile strength that 
have isotropic behavior (R.I. Korsnes, 2008). He studied anisotropic behavior in vertical 
and horizontal, but Talesnick et al. studied the anisotropic behavior of chalk in vertical and 
two planes in horizontal direction, this type of anisotropy is called transvers anisotropy. 
==PAGE:13==
2 
 
This project evaluates the strength of Stevns chalk by conducting series of Brazilian, UCS, 
compressive Triaxial and extension Triaxial tests. Triaxial test are conducted under 
drained conditions while all the samples are fully water saturated.  
All the tests are conducted in ambient temperature and atmospheric pressure. Before 
running tests, physical properties of samples such as porosity, permeability, 𝑃−𝑤𝑎𝑣𝑒 and 
𝑆−𝑤𝑎𝑣𝑒 for classification of samples are measured . Porosity and permeability are 
measured for dry samples while sound measurements are done for fully saturated samples. 
Transvers isotropy is checked for the mechanical properties of Stevns chalk. 
Finally, types of porosities are briefly explained for samples by capturing SEM images. SEM 
images are also captured for failed samples in order to observe changes in porous media 
after failure. 
1-1-Tets Material 
Test material in this project is chalk from Stevns Klint open quarry in Denmark.(See Picture 
1).  
 
Picture 1: Picture taken from the open quarry outside Copenhagen, Denmark. 
==PAGE:14==
3 
 
This chalk in this study is mentioned as a Stevns chalk. Stevns Klint is classified as upper 
Maastrichtian or late Cretaceous period (Håkansson, 1974). Stevens chalk is known for its 
high porosity and its low non carbonate content less than 1% ≈0.5% (Håkansson, 1974) 
as well as its haigh calcite content (> 99%) (Omdal, 2010). Stevns chalk has a low matrix 
permeability (David E. Simon, 1982). The matrix of Stvens chalk consists of  skeleton 
remains of planktonic algae (Cocooliths).  Coccoliths in the stevns chalk are broken into the 
pieces and they formed the porous media which has a larg specific area (𝑆𝑎= 2 𝑚2/𝑔 ). 
Coccoliths could be observed in Picture 2 (K. Hedegaard, 2011).  
 
Picture 2: Structure of Stevns Chalk, magnified 2600x 
Chalk samples which are taken from Stevns Klint open quarry could be classified by  types 
of fracture and induration. Iduration represnts the hardness of rock against heating or 
breaking (Anon., 2015). For this type of sample no fracture obseved in the rock sample so 
fracture could be classified as 𝑆1. For induration stevens chalk is categorized as 𝐻2 or 
slightly indurated, this category specified rock as a material which can be scratched by 
finger nails and easily cut by knife (Andreassen, 2012). 
 
 
==PAGE:15==
4 
 
2- Theory 
2-1-Failure Mechanics 
Failure is happened when a piece of rock exposed to the large stresses. This large stresses 
imply permanent changing of rock’s shape and probably break it. In such a situation the 
capability of rock to carry loads decreases. In petroleum related rock mechanics, failure of 
rock has an important role and it could be cause problem, problem such as mainly borehole 
instability and solids production. Therefore prediction of failure rock behavior is useful to 
prevent borehole instability.  There are four different type of borehole instability: 
- 
Borehole closure: this type of instability narrowing borehole and cause a 
problem such as pipe sticking, difficulty of casings landing and also increase torque and 
drag. 
- 
Borehole enlargement: Borehole enlargement is also called washouts. 
Washouts make hole larger than planned. This undesired phenomena increase difficulty of 
cementing, increase possibility of deviation of well and make problems during logging. 
- 
Fracturing: Fracturing usually happened when the drilling fluid exceeds 
formation pressure. The main problems which happen by fracturing are mud loss 
circulation and possible kick. 
- 
Collapse: collapse is happened when the drilling fluid pressure is less than 
formation pressure. Collapse could convey a problem such as pipe sticking and worse than 
that is loss of well (Aadnoy, 2014). 
Continue this chapter by explanation of some fundamental definition which is use a lot in 
this study. 
 
==PAGE:16==
5 
 
 
Figure 1: Different type of borehole instability

define like equation7 and equation 8 in a general direction (𝜃) which has a relation to the

2-1-4- Strain 
Consider a sample which applies stress on it, if the position of particles, change respect to 
each other (deform) could say sample is strained. Figure 5 represents strain, if points 1 and 
2 assume as a two particles of sample, and 𝐿 is defined as distance between this two points, 
by applying stress on sample, sample is deformed and distance between point 1 and 2 
changes to 𝐿′. Strain could define as: 
𝜀= 𝐿−𝐿′

The sign of strain for compaction is positive, and for extension is negative as initial length is 
smaller than final length.

2-1-5- Strength 
Strength of the rock is commonly defined as a stress level which a rock goes to the failure. 
This stress level is varied for different rocks and could not define it as a unique parameter. 
Strength is a useful parameter when the type of the test, which is applied stress on sample, 
is specified (E.Fjaer, 2008). 
In this study four main tests are carried out. These tests are Brazilian Test, Uniaxial 
compressive strength test (UCS test), Triaxial compressive test and Triaxial Extension test, 
which are the most important tests for measuring the strength of rock. One by one go to the 
detail of each test. The result of the test and boundary condition is mentioned in Section 4-
5- Tests. 
2-1-5-1- Uniaxial compressive strength 
In this type of test, axial stress applies to both end faces of the sample which is cylindrical 
in this study. The axial stress is increased up to the sample goes to the failure. Failure mode 
in this type of test is shear failure. Figure 6 represents result from UCS test which is carried 
out in one of the study’s sample in this project. By plotting axial stress (𝜎𝑎) against axial 
strain (𝜀𝑎) some important concept could be defined: 
 
 
Figure 6: Right: stress on specimen, Left: stress-strain curve for UCS test. 
Elastic region: Deformation of rock in this region is temporary, if the stress release rock 
will back to the initial shape. 
==PAGE:22==
11 
 
Ductile region: Deformation of rock in this region is permanent, but still could support 
load. This region as could be observed is very small. 
Brittle region: Deformation of rock in this region is increase quickly. Rock lost its ability to 
support load.  
Yield point: After this point the permanent changes are occurred and the rock will not 
return to the original state. 
Uniaxial compressive strength (𝑪𝟎): highest axial stress in the test 
2-1-5-2- Triaxial compressive and Triaxial extension test 
Triaxial compressive test is performed by increasing axial stress and radial stress equally 
together up to the some stress level. At this point keep radial stress constant and increase 
axial stress until the failure happens. The other type of Triaxial test is extension. First stage 
of this test is as same as Triaxial compressive. However after the hydrostatic phase (𝜎𝑎=
𝜎𝑟) , keep confining stress constant and decrease axial stress up to the failure. Type of 
failure in former test is mostly shear failure while in the latter the type of failure could be 
varied between shear failure and tensile failure depends on axial and radial stress. Figure 7 
represent the schematic illustration of Triaxial compressive and extension tests. 
(Kwa´sniewski, et al., 2013) 
 
 
Figure 7: Axial stress in compressive is increased (right) while decreased in extension (left), dashed line represent failure line  
==PAGE:23==
12 
 
In the both type Triaxial tests are observed that in high confining stress level in the one 
hand the ability of sample to support a load is increased but on the other hand the stiffness 
of sample decreased. 
In Triaxial test if applied high axial and radial stress in hydrostatic phase another type of 
failure is observed. This type of failure is called pore collapse. Pore collapse is usually 
happened in high porous rock. High porous rock has a skeleton with an open structure as a 
result in high axial and radial stress; grains will be broken and twist into the open space 
(E.Fjaer, 2008). 
2-1-5-3- Brazilian test 
Main purpose of Brazilian test is measure indirect uniaxial tensile strength. Based on the 
theoretical solution constant tensile stress is on the plane in between of compressional 
stress, this phenomenon is the reason of choosing Brazilian test for determining indirect 
tensile strength (Simpson, 2014). Compressional Stress is applied by two steel loading jaws 
on the disc shaped sample (see Figure 8). (R. Ulusay, 2007).For characterizing the reservoir 
rock, tensile strength has an important role. This important role is borehole stability and 
hydraulic fracturing. (R. RISNES, n.d.). Failure condition is represented by Griffith based on 
the oval shape micro cracks for 2D. When the stress level goes beyond some point all the 
micro cracks join to each other and the failure happen, failure type in this test in tensile 
failure.  Tensile strength (𝑇0) could be written as a function of uniaxial compressive 
strength (𝐶0) : 
𝐶0 = 8𝑇0 
12 
The ratio 8 is use based on the experimental procedure. 
Equation13 represents how the tensile strength could be calculated: 
𝑇0 = 0.636 𝐹𝑐
𝐷𝐿 
13 
Where: 
 
𝑇0: Tensile strength (𝑀𝑃𝑎) 
 
𝐹𝑐: Failure point load (𝑁) 
==PAGE:24==
13 
 
 
𝐷: Diameter (𝑚𝑚) 
 
𝐿: Thickness (𝑚𝑚) 
R.Risnes et al. carried out indirect and direct tensile strength test on 47 Aalborg chalk and 
figured out there is a relation between indirect and direct tensile strength as (R. RISNES,

used for explaining failure line. 
 
Figure 8: Stress on sample for Brazilian test 
2-1-6- Tensile failure 
Tensile failure (𝑇0) usually happens when tensile stress applied on sample and go beyond 
some point which can say peak stress. The peak stress called tensile failure. Most 
sedimentary rock like a chalk sample which is used in this project has a low tensile 
strength. When tensile failure happens on a sample, it separates in one or more fracture 
planes. The source of mentioned fracture is existence of some small cracks which are joined 
to each other in the direction of stress applied. If the stress applies perpendicular to the 
existent crack, cracks will close and compact. The principal stress for stress which tensile 
failure is happed could define as (E.Fjaer, 2008): 
𝜎3 = −𝑇0 
15 
==PAGE:25==
14 
 
2-1-7- Shear failure 
When the shear stress apply on the some plane of sample and surpass the critical limit, 
fault zone will grow alongside of this plane. As stress exceed from critical limit, two side of 
fault zone based on the frictional mechanic sliding on each other, this process is called 
shear failure.  Based on the Mohr’s hypothesis critical limit of shear stress is a function of 
normal stress (E.Fjaer, 2008): 
𝜏𝑚𝑎𝑥= 𝑓(𝜎) 
16 
By plotting normal stress against shear stress, based on the equation 16 a line will be 
obtained which is called failure line or failure envelope. Based on the description of Mohr’s 
circle in section 2-1-3- Mohr’s stress circle, principal stress form three circles inside each 
other. If the maximum principal stress increases the big circle which is consist of 
 𝜎1 and 𝜎3 touch the failure line, at this point sample goes to failure. So based on the Mohr’s 
hypothesis shear failure is only depend on max and min principal stress. The highest values 
that sample goes to the failure and touch the failure line in called cohesion and define as 
(E.Fjaer, 2008): 
𝜏𝑀𝑎𝑥= 1
2 (𝜎1 −𝜎3) 
17

2-4-Estimation of Elastic moduli from UCS and Triaxial Test 
In this study two main moduli based on the type of tests are calculated. Like other 
explained part it is assumed the sampled are isotropic and homogeneous. 
2-4-1- Young’s modulus 
Young’s modulus is defined as a parameter which is measured the stiffness of the sample, 
in other word the sample’s resistance against being compressed by axial stress. Based on 
The theory of linear elasticity deals with situations where there are linear relationships 
between applied stresses and resulting strains. In UCS test and Triaxial test Young’s 
modulus are calculated for elastic area which samples behave linearly. There is a linear 
relation between stress (𝜎) and strain (𝜀), which could be written as: 
𝜀= 1
𝐸 𝜎 
38 
Equation 38 is known as Hooke’s law, while the coefficient E is called Young’s modulus or 
Simply the E-modulus. There are several methods to calculate Young’s modulus, for both 
UCS and Triaxial tests Tangent Young’s modulus method is used. In this Method  𝐸𝑡 is 
usually measured at a stress level equal to 50% of failure point (R. Ulusay, 2007). Tangent 
Young’s modulus is illustrated in Figure 12 : 
==PAGE:32==
21 
 
 
Figure 12: Scant Young’s modulus

𝜎3. Hydrostatic phase is mainly performed in this study to determine the bulk modulus of 
the rock before failure point. Bulk modulus in the hydrostatic phase is the slope of stress-
strain curve where the stress axis is defined as an axial stress however strain axis is 
defined as an axial strain plus two times of radial strain, but is assumed samples are 
homogenous and isotropic. So bulk modulus is formulated as bellow:

2-5-Poroelasticity 
Relation between fluid flow and porous medium is mentioned as a poroelasticity. (COMSOL 
group, 2015) However in this project drained tests are carried out but for classification of 
samples Porosity and permeability are measured. 
2-5-1- Porosity 
Porosity is defined as a ratio between pore volume and bulk volume. Porosity is a 
dimensionless parameter as units for nominator and denominator are volume. Usually 
porosity is report as percentage (Society of Petroleum Engineers, 2014). Porosity is 
formulated as below:

in porous medium. Following equation states that permeability could be related to the

2-7-Anisotropy 
Materials have a different behavior and respond in each orientation which stress applies on 
them. This different respond is called anisotropy. There are two type of anisotropy: 
==PAGE:39==
28 
 
2-7-1-Lithological anisotropy 
The origin of this type of anisotropy is in deposition process, in this process grain 
deposited accidentally based on the condition around the sedimentary basin. For example 
in the river, sediments formed and has tendency to orient based on the direction of the 
flow, also the flow rate of river is change the scattering of fine and thicker grain. Thus each 
layer of sedimentary rock in lithological anisotropy has a different grain size and 
arrangement. This type of anisotropy has a direct effect on elastic moduli based on 
direction of the material (E.Fjaer, 2008).     
2-7-2-stress induced anisotropy 
This type of anisotropy is caused by micro cracks which are formed as a result of applying 
stress on sample. Orientation of micro cracks is also important which could effect on the 
compressive strength (Harrison, 1997 ).  
2-7-3-Inhomogeneity  
Inhomogeneity is defined as: having different properties at different location at a certain 
direction while anisotropy generally is defined as having different properties in different 
direction with undetermined location. So the importance of mentioning direction is 
important else these two definitions mixed up. (Harrison, 1997 ) 
The importance of anisotropy in petroleum industry is in drilling and petrophysics 
sections, where the analyzing of the micro cracks orientation help to recognize the 
direction of perforating of well in a way to minimize sand production as well as optimize 
production.  And also could maximize oil recovery from hydraulic fracturing, because if 
micro cracks are opened (fractured) in its direction end up to enhanced oil and gas 
production (T.J. Plona, 2000) . 
==PAGE:40==
29 
 
3- Method and equipment 
3-1-Laboratory Equipment 
All used equipment in this Study to carry out tests is involved of several apparatuses. Most 
of the rock mechanical test laboratory for sedimentary rocks has such equipment. Name of 
equipment which are used to perform a test are as follows: 
3-1-1- ProPerm 
3-1-2- Vacuum desiccator 
3-1-3-Density meter 
3-1-4- Load frame (50𝐾𝑁) 
3-1-5- Brazilian device  
3-1-6- Load frame (45MPa) and confining cell 
3-1-7- Computer for control, record and data processing 
3-1-8- Sound system 
In detail description of equipment is mentioned. 
3-1-1- ProPerm 
This apparatus measures the porosity, grain density and permeability. Nitrogen (N2) 
injects into the core holder which is called the Matrix for measuring porosity. By using 
Boyle’s law, pore volume, bulk volume and grain density are reported in the excel 
spreadsheet. Permeability measurement with this equipment is also reported by injecting 
Nitrogen (N2) to the main core holder. For permeability measurement, ProPerm uses 
Klinkenberg correction in order to calculate real permeability. When gases are used as the 
flowing fluid at low pressures, calculated permeability may be greater than true 
permeability of the rock. In liquid laminar flow, the velocity profile of the liquid is 
Maximum at the center of the passageway and zero at the walls. However, when gas is used 
in the same flow system the gas velocity profile is not zero at the walls, but has a finite 
==PAGE:41==
30 
 
velocity in the direction of flow. Gas diffuses into the space by colliding to the other gas 
molecules, which results change in direction of molecules. Thus, they could never move in a 
straight path. “Mean free path” is defined as average of traveled distances that caused by 
mentioned collisions. At lower pressures, the mean free path is greater, and the distance 
between molecular collisions increases. At any location on a pore’s wall, when no gas 
molecule is in friction (contact) with the pore’s wall, the gas molecules’ movements will be 
result of gas slippage, not pressure difference. The result is that the gas molecules get 
through the porous medium more easily than expected. Therefore, increasing pressure step 
by step make a real friction between pores and gas like friction of liquid and pores, which 
also prevent gas slippage. Gas flow at higher pressures reduces the mean free path, and the 
calculated permeability get closer to the true absolute permeability of the rock. 
Klinkenberg found gas permeability as a function of the gas composition as well as function 
of mean pressure. The equivalent liquid permeability is independent of the two mentioned 
factors (Petroleum engineering department,New Mexico Institute, 2014) . 
 
Picture 3: ProPerm device with name of valves   
==PAGE:42==
31 
 
3-1-2- Vacuum desiccator 
For fully saturating samples by desired fluid, a vacuum desiccator is used in this project. 
Two hose-pipes exit from desiccator; one of them is connected to the vacuum pump and the 
other one is free for sucking desired fluid from fluid container inside the desiccator. 
Connection between pump and fluid container could be opened or closed by installed valve 
on hose-pipe. 
 
 
Picture 4: Vacuum desiccator with name of all connection

This device measures range of density from 0 to 3 g cm3

at temperature from 0 to 90 °C. 
Accuracy of density meter is estimated about 0.00005 g/cm3for density, and 0.03°C for 
temperature. Measurement time is 30 Sec after equilibration (GmbH, 2015).

3-1-4- Load frame (𝟏𝟎𝑲𝑵)  
Capacity of load frame, which was used in this study for Brazilian test, is 10𝐾𝑁 . Load frame 
has a two loading surface, which are parallel to each other. This frame has crosshead lock, 
which could be adjusted in a way to prevent implementing additional unexpected and 
undesired load after failure of specimens. Load frame also has connecting ability to the 
computer and record load, displacement, time and many other parameters that are not 
used in Brazilian test. Load frame plot these parameters against each other in order to help 
observation of the failure load.

3-1-5- Brazilian device 
Brazilian device has two steel loading jaws, which are designed in a way to contact a rock 
with 19.05𝑚𝑚 thickness (height). For Brazilian test in this study, Brazilian device for 
1.5 𝑖𝑛𝑐ℎ samples is designed and manufactured. The drawing of Brazilian device with all 
the dimensions is brought in Appendix 1. Here some important dimensions will be 
mentioned:  
The radius of jaws is 1.5 times of sample’s radius while the width of jaws is 1.1 times of 
samples thickness (height). The other dimensions were scaled based on the Figure 
17(Suggested Methods for Rock Characterization, Testing and Monitoring book page 102).  
Toolox 44, which is modern quenched, tempered pre hardened tool and engineering steel is 
used for manufacturing Brazilian apparatus. Toolox 44 is characterized by a low carbon 
content, which results in a very good machinability. This steel has unique toughness and 
fatigue data, which significantly increases the lifetime of the machine components. The 
typical 
value 
for

modulus 
and 
tensile 
strength 
are 
210 𝐺𝑃𝑎 and 1450 𝑀𝑃𝑎 respectively. Picture 7 displays the prepared Brazilian device for 
Brazilian test.

For conducting Brazilian test, the Brazilian device is mounted between loading surface of 
load frame, and load is applied on jaws.  
3-1-6- Load frame, axial and radial stress 
Load frame is an essential element in the test equipment. This element must consist of 
some important features such as the frame stiffness, Ability to operate in a mode of 
constant displacement rate, maximum operating force in compression , free compression 
space and displacement control (level controller).   
There are two types of load frame used in rock testing: one is a cell where the sample is 
placed between two movable pistons, and the other one that is used in this study has a 
fixed pedestal which carry the sample and a movable pedestal which applying axial stress 
on the sample.  
The axial stress is applied on the specimen by moving axial actuator, which is worked by 
electrical motor. Maximum axial load is 50 𝑀𝑃𝑎 for this load frame. Axial stress could be 
controlled (increased or decreased) by axial level controller. Stress is applied on the piston 
and then piston transfers stress on specimen. Material of pistons should be hard in order to 
tolerate stress.  Used pistons in this study are made of steel, and the flatness of piston’s 
surface is within ±5 𝜇𝑚. The flatness of the pistons has an important effect on the test 
result. If the flatness is above mentioned value, recorded data for sound measurement and 
consequently recording of delay time are wrong. These pistons have also the ability of 
passing through sound wave inside the specimen. There are some small crystals inside 
pistons, which are transducing and receiving sound wave. Sound recording is used to 
measure dynamic parameter.  
On the body of pistons, inlet and outlet vessels are set and used to pump fluid inside and 
drain it to measure pore pressure. Moreover, a socket is set in each piston that connects the 
wire for transferring sound waves from pulse generator and records the received waves by 
oscilloscope. 
In each piston one set of lever is installed; one set is for attaching LVDT, and the other one 
is for attaching plates, which movable shaft of LVTDs are laid on them. LVDT stands for 
==PAGE:46==
35 
 
Linear Variable Differential Transformers, which in this experiment is used for measuring 
strain. Inside of the LVDT,  one primary coil and two secondary coils exist, which are 
surrounding an steel core. LVTD operates when Primary coil is energized by constant 
amplitude A.C. supply. The coil alternates magnetic field in steel core, then induces a 
current into secondary coils and produces voltage. Movements of steel core result in 
changing voltage of secondary coils. Thus, the voltage’s output will be different between the 
two secondary coils. This voltage tells whether the movable shaft is located high or low. 
 
Picture 8: Deferent part of 𝟓𝟎 𝑴𝑷𝒂 load frame  
The axial stress is applied on the sample by moving axial actuator, which works by 
electrical motor. Axial stress could be controlled (increased or decreased) by axial level 
controller. 
Radial stress is applied on the specimen by thick-walled steel, which is called confining cell. 
Confining cell could apply maximum radial load around 64𝑀𝑃𝑎 . Specimen is placed inside 
a cell, which is surrounded by a sleeve that exists inside a steel piston. Inside this cell is full 
of oil that by compressing or decompressing, radial stress on sample will be respectively 
==PAGE:47==
36 
 
increased or decreased. The compressing/decompressing of oil is conducted by the radial 
level controller. Sleeve, which is inside a cell separates sample from the confining fluid. The 
sleeves should be soft enough in order to not provide a significant support to the core. In 
this test, the sleeve is made of rubber and sleeve’s wall is so thin to improve the accuracy of 
radial deformation measurement. 
3-1-7- Computer for control commands, record and data processing 
Load frames ( 10𝐾𝑁 𝑎𝑛𝑑 50𝑀𝑃𝑎) are connected to the computer for controlling, recording 
and data processing. The mentioned actions are done with programs which are called 
Lablog and Merlin: 
3-1-7-1- Lablog 
This software allow operator to write commend for running wanted tests. This program 
provide operator for controlling the load, monitoring the behavior of specimen, recording 
the stress and strain, stop or start the test by writing a command (more explanation are 
brought in 3-2-4-Sound Measurement) and finally recording all the mentioned data as a 
file. This file should be converted to a file with note format. Converting is done by named 
(“LabLogConv”).    
 
Picture 9: Pulse generator and oscilloscope 
==PAGE:48==
37 
 
As mentioned before sound waves could be recorded after passing through the pistons and 
specimen. The waves are sent from transducer to sample and back to the equipment from 
receiver socket. The pulse generator is connected to the oscilloscope for observing 
transduced and received waves. The oscilloscope has the ability to adjust the amplitude of 
wave as well as wave length in order to record the wave in an appropriate wave format. 
The suitable software for recording wave and configuring them is (“Wave acqu”).   
3-1-7-2- Wave acqu 
Wave acquisition is used for recording sound waves; convert them to the raw data 
(number), configure oscilloscope and on top of everything connect oscilloscope to the 
computer.  
In the previous part, it is mentioned that LVTDs are measured strain. This device records 
strain based on voltage, which is generated from LVDT. Voltage should be converted to the 
suitable data. This action is done by the data acquisition device. Data acquisition is 
connected to the channel serial pad. Channel serial pad transfers voltage to the devices 
which need current to function. Then channel serial pad sends the received voltage from 
the device to the data acquisition and converts it to the suitable data. This suitable data is 
transferred to computer. So briefly data acquisition could be defined as a device, which 
interface between computer and devices that send back current or voltage.  
3-1-7-3- Merlin 
This software is used for connecting 10 KN load frame to the computer, as well as 
controlling load.  Merlin is able to record load, displacement, time and many other 
parameters, which are not used in this study. Furthermore, Merlin plot these parameters 
against each other to help observation of the failure point. 
 
 
==PAGE:49==
38 
 
3-2- Experimental procedure 
3-2-1-Collecting, Coring and preparation of samples  
3-2-1-1- Collecting 
As mentioned before all tests are done on the chalk sample, which is collected from Stevns 
Klint field; the costal Stevns Klint is located in eastern part of Denmark. Prominent 
geological significance of this area could be explained as a good outcrop with the 41 meter 
high cliff as well as being one of the best exposed Cretaceous-Tertiary boundaries in the 
world (Surlyk, 2006). This field is located Stevns municipality of Denmark; the coordinate 
of this field is 55°19'22.9"N 12°26'57.0"E (Stevns Kommune, 2014) . 
Seven blocks of Stevns chalk are extracted from the field. Each of these blocks is numbered 
from 1 to 7 and top of each block is marked. The three last samples had the best block 
shape. In Picture 10 extraction’s place and one of the samples can be seen. 
 
 
Picture 10: Left: Extraction place, Right: One of the chalk block, arrow represent top of the block 
All the blocks were wrapped by cling film in order to of prevent evaporating considering 
that all the blocks were saturated by the running sea water in the field. 
==PAGE:50==
39 
 
3-2-1-2- Coring and preparation 
Two chalk blocks were selected out of seven samples, as they had a close shape to the 
rectangular cuboid and coring could be performed easily as well as getting more cylindrical 
samples. 
Before explaining the coring procedure, specific conditions of specimen should be met for 
each test that is presented as follows: 
3-2-1-2-1- Brazilian Test 
The test specimens shall be cylindrical with ratio of 1: 0.5 for Diameter to height. In other 
words height should be approximately equal to the specimens’ radius. The end part of each 
sample should be flat and plane. Furthermore, they shall not depart from vertical axis more 
than ±0.05𝑚𝑚 𝑖𝑛 50 𝑚𝑚 . The sides shall be smooth as well and free of unexpected 
abnormalities and straight to within 0.1 𝑚𝑚. (R. Ulusay, 2007). In order to study about 
anisotropy, cores are taken from three different directions along the 𝑥, 𝑦 𝑎𝑛𝑑 𝑧 axis, which 
they are called Horizontal2 (𝐻2), Horizontal1(𝐻1) and vertical(𝑉) respectively (see Figure 
14). In order to prevent loss of specimens as a result of unexpected incident ten samples 
for each direction are prepared (30 samples in total). 
3-2-1-2-2- Unconfined compressive strength (UCS) Test 
For this test based on the ISRM standards, sample should be cylindrical with a diameter to 
length ratio between 2 and 3. Alternatively it can be said that height of specimen should be 
two times of specimens’ diameter (E.Fjaer, 2008). Both ends of specimen should be flat to 
0.02 mm and should not deviated from vertical axis more than ±0.05mm in 50 mm. Sides 
of specimen should be free of abnormal dent and straight with in 0.3 mm over the whole 
length of sample (R. Ulusay, 2007). In favor of investigation about anisotropy, core are 
taken from three different directions along the x, y and z axes, which they call 
Horizontal2 (H2), Horizontal1(H1) and vertical(V) respectively (see Figure 14). To prevent 
loss of specimens as a result of unexpected incident ten samples for each direction are 
provided (30 samples in total).  
==PAGE:51==
40 
 
3-2-1-2-3- Triaxial Test 
All the specimen’s specifications in this test are similar to UCS test, with the only difference 
in the number of samples. In this part of test for preventing loss of sample due to the 
unexpected incident eight samples for each direction are made (24 samples in total)   
 
Figure 14: Direction of coring for each bulk of chalk 
Figure 14 illustrates how the direction of coring for each bulk of chalk is chosen.    
The procedures of taking core are represented as fallow:  
1- As mentioned before block number 5 and 6 because of having close shape to rectangular 
cuboid are selected. Top of each block carefully marked (See Picture 11). 
2- For taking cores, the used device is stand coring bit with adjustable table. It is impossible 
to put the whole block in the way that sits between table and core bit. So each block divided 
to two or three parts to optimize the number of cylindrical specimens. (See Picture 11) 
==PAGE:52==
41 
 
`
 
 
 
 
Picture 11: Left: Block number 5, Right: Block number 6 
3- Stabilizing block on the table (see the chock in the Picture 12), If the block stays loose on 
the table, it would be shaken. As a result the side of the core will be dented or broken. 
4- Opening the water valve; water acts as a lubricator and allows bit to rotate easily inside 
a sample while drilling. In case of close water valve, on one hand bit penetrates to the block 
very hard and on the other hand core remains inside a core bit.  
==PAGE:53==
42 
 
 
 
Picture 12: Left: block number 5 on the drilling table, red circle is marked chock, Right: block number 6 on the 
drilling table 
4- Before start coring mark direction on top of the place where is planned to drill. Then 
start drilling and prepare cores.   
5- As indicated before cores are taken from 3 directions. For this purpose the middle of 
block is marked horizontally and vertically. As it can be seen at the left side of Picture 12, 
the cores are taken up to middle line.in other words core bit only penetrates to the middle 
line. The core bit penetrates to the middle point in order to leave a space for cores in other 
two directions.  
6- Each core should be cut into the desired size(75𝑚𝑚 higth  for UCS test samples and 
19.05𝑚𝑚 for Brazilian test samples).The special cutter machine is used ,which is designed 
for cutting cores. This device including one core before cutting is shown in Picture 13 :

should be marked again.

==PAGE:57==

In this study, prepared samples were put for 3 days in the oven at 55°C. Samples were 
weighed each day to recognize whether they are dried well or not. In this case, the 
difference of sample’s weight between 2nd and 3rd day of drying process was zero, which 
means samples were dried completely. Method by ASTM D22 16 suggested putting sample 
in the oven at 110°C for one day and then measures the sample’s weight. This method is 
very precise however; some organic material might be dissolved by drying in the 
mentioned temperature. 
 
Picture 16: two batches of prepared sample inside a oven at 𝟓𝟓°𝑪 
The following steps were done to weigh samples: 
1- Before start weighing, balance needs to be "tared," or recalibrated to read 0.000 𝑔.  
2- Put sample in the balance. 
3- Wait until displayed number become constant. 
4- Record displayed number as a weight of sample. 
The last important part for preparation of samples is measuring the height and diameter. 
The importance could be summarized as if these measurements are carried out wrong, next 
steps will be affected and result will be reported with an error.  Measurements of height 
==PAGE:58==
47 
 
and diameter are done three times for each sample and the mean value of three 
measurements are reported. Three times measurement are implemented in order to 
reduce error. Source of error in measurement is existence of dent in samples. 
In the section 4-1- Drying, weighing and basic measurement , measuring size of samples 
and their weights (include weight of samples during drying procedure) are reported. 
3-2-2-Porosity and permeability Measurement 
As previously mentioned porosity and permeability are measured by Properm. For 
measuring porosity, this device reports bulk volume (𝑉𝑏), pore volume (𝑉𝑝) and grain 
Volume (𝑉𝑔𝑟) by simple calculation, which is mentioned in the equation 40, Therefore 
porosity could be calculated. By running proper for measuring permeability, device reports 
gas permeability (𝐾𝑔) and liquid permeability (𝐾𝐿). 𝐾𝐿 is a reliable value for using as a 
permeability. As mentioned before in the high pressure friction of gas is like liquid friction 
so the real permeability is measured. The other values such as inlet pressure, outlet 
pressure and fluid flow are also reported in an excel file. These values indicate that in each 
steps which pressure value should be used, and also whether operator is on the wright 
path or not.    
3-2-2-1- Porosity measurement 
Required steps in porosity measurement process are as follows: 
1- Reset PAtm. 
2- Load the sample in the matrix. 
3- Reduce the free volume in matrix by loading provided suitable billets. 
4- Wipe the seal of the matrix with finger to remove small particles which are blocked 
nuzzles. 
5- Close matrix 
6- Set the valves as follow: 
==PAGE:59==
48 
 
 
6-1-Source valve is ON. 
 
6-2-Matrix valve is set toward Vent. 
 
6-3-Backward / Forward valve is set toward Forward. 
 
6-4-Pressure / Vent valve in set toward Vent. 
 
6-5-Inlet valve of core holder is set as closed 
8- Input data in black cells of area B in AppliLab. Select the measure GV in Area C, tick the 
billets which are loaded in matrix and then click START. 
9- After START button is pressed, pop-up windows will guide operator.1 
3-2-2-2- Permeability 
Required stages for measuring permeability are as follows: 
1- Reset PAtm. 
2- Load the sample (cylindrical shape) in the core sample. 
3- Set the valves as follows: 
 
3-1-Source valve is ON 
 
3-2-Matrix valve is set toward Vent 
 
3-3-Backward / Forward valve is set toward Backward in order to measure the KL 
in 5 steps by increasing back pressure. 
 
3-4-Pressure / Vent valve is set toward Pressure. Manometer shows approximately 
 
3-5-350 psi / 24 bar Inlet and Outlet valve at core holder are open. 
4- Input data in black cells of area B, select the required mode in Area C and then click 
START. 
                                                        
1 Manual handbook of Properm equipment   
==PAGE:60==
49 
 
5- After START button is pressed, pop-up windows will guide operator. 
6- Once measure is completed for the first step, data is saved in an Excel sheet, then change 
the back pressure for second step. 
7- Back pressure is changed by screw the red knob which is known as a metering valve.  
8- Enter the dial reading in the metering valve (red knob) to the AppliLab. 
9- Changing the flow rate to increase the inlet and outlet pressure difference.  
10- Repeat items 7-9 for each step. In the fifth step the liquid permeability is reported. 2  
With ProPerm device the permeability of samples with 19.05 𝑚𝑚 could not measured.  
3-2-3-Saturation of selected samples with vacuum desiccator 
For saturating the selected sample the following steps are conducted. 
1- Breaking one extra 75 mm sample by hammer and grind it. 
2- Make a solution by mixing chalk powder and distilled water. 
 
Picture 17: mixture solution of distilled water and chalk powder 
3-Density of produced solution is measured by using the ‘’Density meter’’. The following 
stages are done to get the density:  
 
3-1- First, clean all the tubes and equipment that are inside the device using 
methanol and toluene. Then evacuate the device from chemical agent.  
                                                        
2 Manual handbook of Properm equipment   
==PAGE:61==
50 
 
 
3-2- For measurement, first run the device while there is no fluid injected inside it, 
therefore, the device should report density of air which is equal to 0.001225 𝑔/𝑐𝑚3 . If this 
number does not show on the screen, it means there is still some fluid inside the device. 
Cleaning required until the reported number is equal to density of air. By assurance of the 
device cleanness, inject mixing solution and start pumping. Wait for a while (around 30 
sec) until the density is reported. 
3-3- The density is reported for produced mixed solution at 21°𝐶 as 0.9983 𝑔/𝑐𝑚3 . 
 
Picture 18: Density meter desplay density of air  
4- Put the samples on the white perforated shelf which is inside the desiccator. 
 
Picture 19: Selected samples on perforated shelf 
==PAGE:62==
51 
 
5- Start vacuuming the desiccator for 30min by vacuum pump. 
6- Usually fluid flows from a place with high pressure to a place with low pressure. 
Consider this fact to fill desiccator with desired fluid. Open the valve of pipe, which one end 
is in desiccator and the other end is inside the Erlenmeyer flask that contains the mixture 
solution. 
 
Picture 20: vacuum desiccator, vacuum pump and mixture solution 
7- Fill the vacuum container with mixture solution up to the 1 cm above the white 
perforated shelf. The other way is to fill the container with mixture solution up to the point 
that only 1cm of samples are flooded into the saltwater. At this point close the valve. 
 
Picture 21: Mixture solution is filled, up to 1cm above the perforated shelf 
8- Keep vacuuming for 10 minutes and repeat this procedure of vacuuming for half a day. 
While only 1 cm of sample is flooded in the mixture solution, keep vacuuming. Based on 
==PAGE:63==

capillary forces the sample is saturated by mixture solution. All the mixture solution is 
absorbed by chalk sample based on capillary force.  
 
Picture 22: Mixture solution is absorbed completely by chalk 
9-Again fill the container with mixture solution up to the point that only half of the 0.75" 
samples flooding in mixture solution. Continue vacuuming for half day.  
10- After 2 days by repeating the following procedure sample were completely flooded in 
mixture solution. Until flooding of samples is completed, keep vacuuming for 3 more days. 
Every day the samples were weighed and then percentage of saturation was calculated 
based on the formula which is mentioned in section 4-3- Saturation.  
 
Picture 23: Samples are flooded in mixture solution 
10- To prevent evaporating of mixture solution during weighing, samples were wrapped 
around a moist cloth which was moistened by the same saturated fluid of samples.

3-2-4-Sound Measurement  
For samples’ classification plus measuring porosity, bulk density and permeability, the 
other parameter could help classification is sound measurement. This measurement is 
done before the Brazilian test, UCS test and Triaxial Test. Wave propagation in samples is 
recorded by conducting the following steps:   
1- Wrap a layer of cling film around the specimens in order to lose the saturation as little as 
possible during recording wave propagation in the samples. 
2- By level controller adjust the space between loading point (upper loading face) and the 
lower part, which is the bottom of the cell. This space should be proper enough to put the 
loading pistons, billets and 19.05𝑚𝑚 or 75 𝑚𝑚 specimens. Sound measurement procedure 
is similar to the procedures mentioned in section 3-2-6-Uniaxial compressive strength Test. 
The differences are: 
 
2-1- In scripts add command “wait for Operator”. This command allows operator to 
make additional measurement such as record wave propagation through the specimens. 
Axial load of 1𝑀𝑃𝑎 with constant rate of 1.5𝑚𝑚/ℎ is applied on the specimens.  
 
2-2- Attach transducer and receiver cables from the pulse generator and 
oscilloscope to the upper and lower pistons respectively. Cables are attached exactly after 
fixing pistons and specimen by applying the small load about 150𝐾𝑃𝑎 . Usually transducer 
cable attaches to the upper piston and receiver cable attaches to the lower piston.  
 
2-3- For sound measurement there is no necessity to measure the strain in 
specimens, consequently LVDTs are not used for measuring wave propagation.( See Picture 
24) 
3- By appearance of ‘’Wait for operation’’ command, record the sound wave. For recording 
the sound wave enter to the program ‘’ Wave acqu’’, go to setup and fill the required 
information such as name of samples and date. Then configure the oscilloscope in order to 
record the correct ranges of signals for pressure velocity and shear velocity. In this 
==PAGE:65==
54 
 
program the recording of the velocity should be adjusted on the ‘’manual’’ mode for 
recording the sound velocity in desired moments. 
4- After recording wave propagation and releasing the system, put the samples inside 
saturating solution and use recorded data for interpretation. Data was automatically saving 
during the measurement of wave propagation and could be directly used without any need 
to converting like data recorded by “LabLog”.

3-2-4-1- System delay measurement 
Theoretically, if the transducer and receiver cables directly attach to each other, meaning 
that no specimen is located between the transducer and the receiver, similar wave that is 
transduced from transducer should be recorded by receiver. However, the generated 
waveform that is effectively induced into the specimen is generally different because of the 
dead time. Dead time is defined the time required for wave to transfers through the cable 
and between pistons’ surfaces (sensors that propagate and receive waves) and specimen 
(CAMACHO-TAUTA, et al., 2012). Delayed time should be measured and taken into account 
when pressure velocity and shear velocity calculating. The procedures, which are done for 
calculating delayed time were exactly like pervious section, except the fact that steel billets 
with different lengths which are mentioned Table 3, were used instead of chalk specimen 
(steel sample number 6  is made by putting billet number 4 over billet number 5).  
Sample no. 
Length(mm) 
4 
12.66 
5 
25.4 
6 
38.06 
7 
50.85 
Table 3: Number of steel sample and their length 
 
 
Figure 15: Steel billets for measuring delay time 
4

3-2-5-Indirect tensile strength by Brazilian Test 
Brazilian test is planned to measure uniaxial tensile strength indirectly. The experimental 
fact shows that most of the rock fails in the tension along perpendicular axis to the axial 
stress; needless to say that axial stress is in compressive load format. By using this fact the 
tensile strength could be measured indirectly.  
The following procedures are conducted for Brazilian test. 
1- As mentioned before all the samples are saturated. In order to prevent loose saturation 
all the Brazilian samples were carried in the bucket of saturated water. 
2- For each direction 5 test specimens with circle surface were prepared. However during 
sound measurement one sample at each direction is failed which results in conducting test 
with 4 specimens in each direction. During coring of specimens the direction wrote down 
on the surface of specimen. In this test, it is important to know in what direction load on 
samples is applied. Therefore, one could measure tensile strength in two other directions 
by rotating sample. For instance if a test is run for one sample in vertical direction tensile 
strength in directions of Horizontal1 and Horizontal 2 can be measured. Figure 16 
illustrates the mentioned possibility of tensile strength measurement in different 
directions. 
3- One layer of masking tape was wrapped around sample. Masking tape helps specimen 
mounted squarely in Brazilian device and load could be equally applied to each part of 
specimen. 
4- Load frame could be controlled manually by level controller and automatically by 
computer. Load frame is connected to computer by the software called Merlin. Brows 
mentioned program, in the first window there are two boxes which they can adjust load, 
time of running test and time-load chart. In this program define name of sample, type of 
sample which in cylindrical, diameter and height of cylindrical sample. 
5- The sample with the desired direction was put in between Brazilian device’s jaws and 
then it was installed on the loading surface. Manually movable loading surface was 
==PAGE:68==
57 
 
adjusted on the top of ball bearing until a little load on specimen was observed in the 
program.    
 
Figure 16: Possibility of tensile strength measurement in different directions  
 6- Load on specimen should be adjusted in a way that failure occurs within 15 −30 𝑆𝑒𝑐 . 
Loading rate for all the specimens is set on 0.8 𝐾𝑁/𝑚𝑖𝑛.  
7- A test by click on the start bar in the program was started; the time-load graph was 
observed. Immediately after detection of crack on specimen the test was stopped. The data 
was save and procedure was continued for other specimens. 
==PAGE:69==
58 
 
 
 
Picture 25: Left: specimen in between of Brazilian device’s jaws after failure, Right: specimen in between of Brazilian device’s 
jaws before failure  
The left side of Picture 25 illustrates how sample is failed by highlighting the crack path on 
surface of sample V5. On the bottom left side of this picture the way a sample mounted in 
Brazilian device is demonstrated.  
According to Picture 25, practice how applied Figure 16 on sample V5. As it observes in this 
picture, load is applied along the written name on the sample(blue arrows in Figure 16 ), so 
the tensile strength is along the horizontal 1 axis(green arrows in Figure 16), therefore 
could easily say the tensile strength along horizontal 1 axis is obtained. Tensile strength for 
other samples is measured like this procedure as well. The pictures for rest of samples 
which Brazilian test applied on them are mentioned in Appendix 2. 
Two main apparatus of this test are suitable load frames which implement compressive 
stress and two steel loading jaws (Brazilian device). Brazilian device is designed in a way to 
contact a rock with 19.05𝑚𝑚 thickness (height). For Brazilian test in this study, Brazilian 
device for 1.5 𝑖𝑛𝑐ℎ samples is designed and manufactured. The drawing of Brazilian device 
with all the dimensions is in Appendix 1.Here several important dimensions are presented 
as follows.  
the radius of jaws is 1.5 times of sample’s radius while the width of jaws is 1.1 times of 
samples thickness (height). The other dimensions were scaled based on the Figure 18 (The 
ISRM Suggested Methods for Rock Characterization, Testing and Monitoring book page 
102)  
==PAGE:70==
59 
 
 
Figure 17: Brazilian device 
Toolox 44 which is a modern quenched, tempered pre hardened tool and engineering steel 
was used for manufacturing Brazilian apparatus. Toolox 44 is characterized as a low 
carbon content, which results in a very good machinability. This steel has unique toughness 
and fatigue data, which increase the lifetime of the machine’s components significantly. The 
typical value for Young’s modulus is about 210 𝐺𝑃𝑎 (SAAB, 2003) .Picture 7 displays the 
prepared Brazilian device for the Brazilian test. 
 
Picture 26: Brazilian Device 
 The second apparatus for conducting Brazilian test is load frame. The capacity of load 
frame, which was used in this study is 10𝐾𝑁 . Load frame has a two loading surface which 
are parallel to each other. This frame has crosshead lock, which could be adjusted in a way 
to prevent implementing additional unexpected and undesired load after failing specimens. 
Load frame also has ability to record load, displacement, time and many other parameters 
which are not used in Brazilian test.  
==PAGE:71==
60 
 
3-2-6-Uniaxial compressive strength Test 
The main purpose of applying UCS test in this study is to determined compressive 
strength (𝐶0) , stress-Strain curve and Young’s modulus. Procedures of running USC test 
are explained in the following steps:  
1- By using level controller adjusting the space between loading point (upper loading face) 
and the lower part, which is bottom of the cell. This space should be large enough to put the 
loading pistons, billets and specimen. This procedure is as follows: 
 
1-1- press Reset button to observe command ‘’Function?’’ in the level controller’s 
screen. 
 
1-2- press DOWN button for increasing the space or could be described as the 
button which sends signals to the load frame and decreases the load on specimen. 
 
Picture 27: Axial loading level controller 
2- Put the billet on the center of bottom face of the load cell. On the bottom face some 
circles are carved, billet should be placed in the center of carved circle (See Picture 28, 
number 1). 
==PAGE:72==
61 
 
3- Two plates are installed on the bottom piston. On the installed plates, movable shaft of 
LVTDs are laid. This piston should be put on the billet which is set in the center of bottom 
face and check the verticality of this piston. (See Picture 28, number 2) 
4- Wrap a cling film around the specimen for not losing saturation, then put it on top of the 
mentioned piston. Specimen should be situated in the center of piston in order to apply 
load equally.     
5- Put another piston with the levers, which holds LVTDs on the top of specimen. This 
piston also should be placed on center of specimen. (Picture 28, number 3)  
6- Put the billet on the top of the piston with levers. This billet should be laid on the center 
of the piston. (Picture 28, number 4) 
 
Picture 28: Loading pistons and billets 
7- Check the verticality of pistons and specimen by sprite level. System must be quite 
vertical with the purpose of applying load to both ends of the specimen equally. In case of 
sound measurement, carved lines on the piston should be exactly along with each other to 
1 
2 
4 
3 
==PAGE:73==
62 
 
record waves. In other words the installed sockets on the pistons should be along with a 
certain line.       
8- By level controller apply a small load to the whole system of billets, pistons and 
specimen one more time. this procedure is as follows: 
 
7-1- Press Reset button to observe command ‘’Function?’’ in the level controller’s 
screen. 
 
7-2- Press ‘’Up’’ bottom for decreasing the space or increasing the load on specimen. 
In this stage, verticality of the system could be also checked. When the loading point’s face 
is closed to the top billet, loading face and billet should be parallel to each other. If the 
system is not adjusted vertically, they will not parallel. In this regards, Picture 29 
demonstrates the way that billet and loading face should be parallel. 
 
Picture 29: Billet and loading face are parallel to each other 
 
7-3- Increase the axial load up to 150KPa. in this load the installed system is being 
kept firm. When the number 150 shows on the level controller’s screen, click on the 
‘’Stop/Cont’’ button to stop the movement of loading point.   
==PAGE:74==
63 
 
 9- LVDTs are attached to the free levers. Moveable shaft of LVDT should be placed on the 
plate which is installed on the bottom piston, in a way that approximately 1cm of shaft be 
exposed from the main body of LVTD. Generally it should be adjusted in a way that output 
voltage stands between minimum and maximum output. If this value does not stand 
between these ranges, the LVTD could not report correct values. LVTD also should be 
installed and adjusted vertically for measuring the strain without any error. 
Perpendicularity could be checked by using spirit level and its vertical should also be 
checked.(see Picture 30) 
10-Press ‘’Enter’’ and ‘’Reset’’ buttons on the level controller together. The appeared word 
‘’Function?’’ on the level controller’s screen means that the load frame is ready to receive 
command from “lab log”. 
 
 
 
 
Picture 30: Left: whole system of billets, pistons, wrapped specimen and LVDTs, Right: Position of LVDT on the plate and 
checking verticality of LVDT 
 
==PAGE:75==

11- Enter to the ‘’lab log’’ program and do the following procedure: 
 
11-1- When the program is opened it takes a while for data acquisition to start 
functioning. In opened windows desired parameters such as length, Diameter, name of 
project, sample number and etc. are defined in allocated boxes. 
 
11-2- Load one of the previous setup and adjust all the connection and change them 
if necessary. In Setup for the UCS test the main hook cell, data acquisition and two LVDTs 
are defined. 
 
11-3- Check the connection of LVDTs. In this test 6V current for sending voltage to 
LVTD is used. Mentioned current is sent by channel 1. LVDT number 104 connect to 
channel 2 and LVDT number 105 connect to channel 3. 
 
Picture 31: Channel series pad, channel number and connections  
 
11-4- close the connection panel and click on the ‘’continue the test’’ tab. Enter into 
the page that the appropriate script for controlling the axial load could be written. In this 
test, the script is written for applied load on the specimen up to its failure. For UCS test, 
Load on the specimen should be applied constantly with a stress rate that causes sample’s 
failure within 5 −10 𝑚𝑖𝑛. Based on running dummy test on spare samples in all three 
directions, samples went to failure at the stress level below 3𝑀𝑃𝑎 while the constant rate 
was 4.25 𝑚𝑚/ℎ, which is equal to 5.6% length of samples. An appropriate script was 
written based on above information.    
 
11-5- By clicking on the ’’Execute’’ tab in the program, the written scrip runs.

11-6- Observe the stress-strain curve, which is plotted while test is running. As soon 
as drop appearance in the graph sample is failed. Wait for a while to make sure this 
fluctuation is result of failure, not an error in LVDTs measurement. If graph shows a 
dropping trend, sample’s failure is being proved. Click on the ’’Execute’’ tab for entering 
into the next step of command, which is unloading. Click on the “End test” tab to finish the 
test and save the recorded data. 
12- For releasing whole system, Click ‘’Enter’’ and ‘’Reset’’ buttons on the level controller 
together. The word ‘’Function?’’ appears on the level controller screen, which means 
connection between computer and load frame is cut off. Load on the sample is decreased by 
Pressing ‘’Down’’ button on the level controller. When the stress is completely removed on 
the sample, click ‘’Stop/Cont’’ button to stop movement of loading point. Finally, click on 
the ‘’Reset’’ button to prepare level controller for next operation. 
13- Take the recorded data from ‘’lab log’’ for interpreting. Recorded data from ‘’lab log’’ 
should be converted by the program called ‘’lab log convertor’’.

3-2-7-Triaxial Compressive and Triaxial Extension Test 
The main purposes of Triaxial Compressive and Triaxial Extension Test in the study 
presented here, are to determine Stress-Strain curve, Young’s modulus and Bulk modulus 
(Hydrostatic phase). Procedures of running Triaxial Compressive and Triaxial Extension 
Test are explained as follow: 
1- Wrap a layer of cling film around the specimen. 
2- Insert specimen inside of the confining cell. Specimen should be sited in the middle of 
confining cell. 
3- Inset two pistons inside a cell, some direct lines curved on the pistons, which should be 
along each other. 
6- Press ‘’Reset’’ button on confining cell’s level controller, then press “Empty’’ button. The 
confining stress around pistons and sample is increased, as soon as the confining stress on 
level controller shows load values around 170 KPa, stop filling the cell. Click ‘’Stop/cont’’ 
button and then click ‘’Reset’’ and ’’Enter’’ buttons together to make the level controller 
ready for receiving command from computer. At this stress, the specimen and pistons are 
kept firm inside a confining cell. Usually at stress levels which are less than 170KPa the 
confining cell slips, and position of the cell is changes. 
 
 
Picture 32: Left: Confining cell and inserted specimen and two pistons inside it, Right: radial stress controller 
==PAGE:78==
67 
 
7- Similar to UCS test, the specimen and pistons, which are kept by confining cell are put 
between the two metal billets. By using spirit level make sure that the whole parts of 
system are quiet vertical. 
8- Manually by clicking on axial level controller’s ‘’up’’ button increase the axial stress up 
to 150KPa, under this stress the installed system is kept firm. When the number 150𝐾𝑃𝑎 
shows on the level controller’s screen, click on the ‘’Stop/Cont’’ button to stop loading point 
movements.   
 9- Attach LVDTs like the ninth step of the procedure in section ( 3-2-1-2-2- Unconfined 
compressive strength (UCS) Test)  
 
 
Picture 33: Left: Checking verticality of LVDT and Right: Checking verticality of confining cell 
11- Press “Enter” and “Reset” buttons together for starting controlling Triaxial cell by 
computer. 
12- Enter into the ‘’lab log’’ program and do the following procedure: 
 
12-1- When the program is opened it takes a while for data acquisition to start 
functioning. Next desired parameters such as length, Diameter, name of project, sample 
number and etc. are defined in the allocated boxes. 
==PAGE:79==
68 
 
 
12-2- Load one of the previous setup and adjust all the connections. Furthermore 
add all devices, which are used such as main hook cell, confining cell, and two LVDTs. 
 
12-3- Adjust the connection of LVDTs, which are same as UCS test. 
 
12-4- close the connection panel and click on the ‘’continue the test’’ tab. Enter into 
the window that the appropriate script for controlling the axial and radial load could be 
written. In this test, two scripts are written; one for Triaxial compressive test and the other 
one for Triaxial extension test. Before running Triaxial test, run hydrostatic test for 
estimating pore collapse failure point. In this study, mainly works were on tensile failure 
(Brazilian test and extension Triaxial test) and shear failure (UCS test and Compressive 
Triaxial test), therefore, commands for compressive and extension Triaxial test are written 
for applying load below the pore collapse failure point. Script for compressive and 
extension Triaxial test are written as follows: 
 
12-4-1- Triaxial Compressive test: Axial and Radial stress increase hydrostatically 
up to 1.25 MPa (for samples V6, H16, H26) and 1.75 MPa (for samples V7, H17, H27). Set 
axial loading rate1%/ℎ of height of sample, in other words axial loading rate is set 
at 0.75 𝑚𝑚/ℎ . For next step keep radial stress constant at 1.25 MPa (for samples V6, H16, 
H26) and 1.75 MPa (for samples V7, H17, H27) and increase axial stress up the failure point.  
 
12-4-2- Triaxial extension test: Axial and Radial stress increase hydrostatically up 
to 3 MPa (for samples V8, H18, H28) and 5.5 MPa (for samples V9, H19, H29). Axial loading 
rate is set as 1%/ℎ of sample’s height. In other words is set at 0.75 𝑚𝑚/ℎ . For next step 
keep radial stress constant at 3 MPa (for samples V8, H18, H28) and 5.5 MPa (for samples 
V9, H19, H29) and decrease axial stress up the failure point. 
Observe the stress-strain curve, which is plotted while test is running. As soon as the graph 
shows a drop in Compressive and an increase in extension, sample is failed. Wait for a 
while to make sure this fluctuation is result of failure not an error in LVDTs measurement. 
Click on the ’’Execute’’ tab for entering the next step of command, which is unloading. Click 
on the “End test” tab to finish the test and save the recorded data.  
==PAGE:80==
69 
 
    13- For releasing system, press ‘’Enter’’ and ‘’Reset’’ buttons together on axial stress level 
controller till word ‘’Function?’’ appears on the level controller screen. Push ‘’Down’’ button 
to decrease the stress on the system. Click ‘’Stop/Cont’’ button to stop movement of loading 
point, when the stress is completely removed from the system. Bring out the system and 
lay down the confining cell as shown at the left side of Picture 32, Press “Enter’’ and ‘’Reset’’ 
buttons together on radial stress level controller till word ‘’Function?’’ appears on the level 
controller’s screen. Decrease the radial stress on the system by Pressing ‘’Empty’’ button 
and then remove the specimen and pistons. 
14- Take the recorded data from ‘’lab log’’ and do the further analyses on recorded data. 
Recorded data from ‘’lab log’’ should be converted by the program called ‘’lab log 
convertor’’.

3-2-8-Scanning Electron Microscopy (SEM) 
The scanning electron microscope (SEM) is one of the most useful devices for checking and 
analyzing of the microstructure and chemical composition. (Weilie Zhou, 2007).  
A scanning electron microscope scans a gathered electron beam pixel on pixel on a surface 
to create an image. (Anon., 2015). Electron is diffused from thermionic electron gun 
(filament) which means it heats up and scattered bunch of electrons. Beam of electron is 
induced down to the specimen. Beam of electron pass through the electromagnets 
(condenser lens) to focus exactly on the specimen. Electron directly moving toward the 
specimen, as specimen has a positive charge.  
 
 
Figure 18: Left: schematic diagram of SEM (James H. Wittke, 2008), Right: SEM device 
When the electron beam hit the surface of specimen, two types of electrons come off, one 
type is secondary electrons, which come from atoms that have absorbed the energy of the 
electron beam, the secondary detector that has a positive charge collect this type of 
electrons and use them to create an image on the computer’s screen. The other type of 
electrons is back scatter electrons. Back scatter electrons are those electrons which are 
reflecting off the surface and deeper from within the specimen. Mentioned electrons could 
==PAGE:82==
71 
 
be detected by back scatter detector. Secondary electrons come from the surface of the 
specimen which is very shallow but very good for getting surface features. The back scatter 
electrons come from deeper within specimen and reflected electron. There is also another 
type of electrons, which never come back to the detector and get trapped in the specimen 
and radiate X-rays. This type cannot be detected by SEM. (Anon., 1998-2015) 
For taking a picture following procedures are done: 
1- Samples for SEM should be prepared. Some prepared specimens can be seen in Picture 
34. Picture 34 a, shows intact samples in vertical, Horizontal 1, Horizontal 2 directions and 
Picture 34 b, demonstrates samples which are failed in Brazilian test, UCS test and Triaxial 
tests.  
Intact samples are cut while their surface is perpendicular to the axis’ direction.  SEM 
samples which are prepared from failed sample are cut in a way that their surface is 
perpendicular to the axial stress. (See Picture 34 c and d) 
 
 
 
 
Picture 34: a): Prepared samples in different direction, b): Prepared test samples after failure, c): Place of prepared sample 
based on directions in intact sample, d): Place of prepared sample based on axial stress   
a) 
b) 
c) 
d) 
==PAGE:83==
72 
 
2- Put samples on the specimen holder which is installed on the specimen stage. 
 
Picture 35: Specimens on the specimen holder 
3- Start vacuuming inside the chamber which specimen stage is in it. Vacuuming is done 
for removing air from the electrons. The vacuum is employed up to 110 𝑃𝑎. 
4- Find an appropriate area for scanning, and then capture a picture.

4-Result and discussion 
In this section the results of all the performed tests are mentioned, for each part the 
possible interpretation of data are achieved and finally the behavior of rock failure 
mentioned. In this project assumed that samples are isotropic, homogenous and has linear 
elastic behavior. Based on this assumption interpretation of data for Brazilian test, UCS 
test, Triaxial compressive test and Triaxial extension test in this chapter are made.

project. The entire sample dried for three days in oven, bar charts the in Figure 19-Figure 
24, illustrated the weight of samples before and after drying and the percent of changing 
weight in sample during drying procedure.

The first three figures are for first series of samples, as could be observed the weights of 
samples are decreased in each day of weighing. In the second series of sample the same 
trend could be observed but the only difference is the percentage of losing water during 
drying procedure. The average percentage value of changing weight during assessing for 
fist series is 8.6% while for second series estimated as17.30%. It means the second series 
of samples were saturated with water more than first series, the reason is first series of 
sample prepared sooner than the second series and keep at temperature room one day 
more than second series and water is evaporated at temperature room and then in the 
same time put both series in the oven. 
The above figures also represent that for 75𝑚𝑚 samples the final weight is 
between121𝑔−128𝑔 where this value for 19.05𝑚𝑚 samples is 28𝑔−32𝑔 . It means the 
prepared samples have a more or less same height and diameter (bulk volume) thus their 
bulk density, grain density (see Appendix 3 and Table 4) and their porosity is more or less 
same.

Figure 26 and Figure 27 illustrate high value of porosity for 19.05 𝑚𝑚 samples in 
comparison with 75 𝑚𝑚 samples. Difference can be observed in porosity between 
19.05 𝑚𝑚 and 75 𝑚𝑚 samples while they are from same directions, this difference can be 
explained as a measurement procedure of porosity for 19.05 𝑚𝑚 samples. Free volume in 
matrix should be filled by loading billet inside the matrix, for samples with the mentioned 
length matrix was filled with 3 billets. As a result there are gaps between the billets, which 
are put on top of each other. These gaps measured as a pore volume and entered to the 
porosity calculation, thus calculated porosity is higher than the real value. 
As mentioned in the theory section, to some extend most of the sedimentary rocks are 
anisotropic and have a different elastic behavior, which results in different strength 
orientations. Porosity is a function of rock strength, which is formulated by power law (R. 
A. FARQUHAR, 1993); rock with high porosity has a low strength and vice versa. Therefore, 
for minimizing effect of porosity in our strength calculation and other mechanical 
properties, samples with close porosity to each other were chosen for different directions. 
For each direction samples within 0.5% difference in porosity were selected. Figure 19 the 
porosity of 1st and 2nd series of samples are plotted for vertical, horizontal 1 and horizontal 
2 directions. Red dots represent the samples which are selected and their porosity has 
difference within 0.5% .

As can be seen in above figures the range of porosity for 75𝑚𝑚 samples is 43.95% −
44.45%  and for  19.05𝑚𝑚 samples is 45.5% −46%. There is about 3% difference between 
porosity of 19.05 𝑚𝑚 samples and 75 𝑚𝑚 samples due to the porosity measurement error 
in Brazilian samples (19.05 𝑚𝑚). Summary of mentioned information for chosen samples 
are in Appendix 6. R.I.Korsnes estimates the average porosity of Stevns chalk 
is 48.18% and 47.70% for vertical and horizontal direction respectively. Porosity of Stevns 
chalk specimens in this study is lower about 8% and 4% for vertical and horizontal 
directions respectively, in comparison with R.I.Korsnes’s study. (R.I. Korsnes, 2008)

Klindenburge demonstrates that the gas permeability decreases by increasing mean 
pressure and vice versa, if plotting 𝐾𝑔 against 1 𝑃̅
⁄   , intercepts of trend line represents 𝐾𝑙 .

Table 5: Permeability of selected samples, accuracy of measurement for𝑲𝒈= 𝟎. 𝟏𝟓𝒎𝒅 and for 𝑲𝒍= 𝟎. 𝟏𝟒 𝒎𝒅 
Table 5 represents that permeability in vertical direction are different from horizontal 
directions. However, there is a small difference between horizontal1 and horizontal2 
permeability, which is due to the error in measurement and is negligible.  
Type of mineral and grain size change permeability in different parts of a rock. Measuring 
permeability for parallel sedimentary layer may be different from permeability 
measurement for layer that is perpendicular to the sedimentary layer. Thus, permeability 
measurement in vertical direction is different from horizontal 1 and horizontal2 directions. 
This directional dependency could be defined as anisotropy. The ratio between vertical 
permeability and horizontal permeability (𝐾𝑣𝐾ℎ
⁄
) is called permeability anisotropy. 
Anisotropy in permeability that must be taken into account in the procedure which fluids 
with different density are exist, such as water flooding, gas injection for oil recovery. 
Permeability anisotropy  also has an effect on well completion and fracturing. Based on the 
result of Morecambe gas field, low permeability anisotropy represents high recovery in 
==PAGE:94==
83 
 
reservoir, which means there is an inverse relation between 𝐾𝑣𝐾ℎ
⁄
 and recovery of 
reservoir. (Cosan Ayan, 1994)  
The average permeability for vertical, horizontal1 and horizontal 2 are: 
𝐾𝑣= 4.41 𝑚𝑑 
𝐾ℎ1 = 7.12𝑚𝑑 
𝐾ℎ2 = 7.04𝑚𝑑 
By the following values the recovery of reserve in Morecambe gas field is about 400 𝑏𝑐𝑓. 
However, the point that formation of this field is sandstone should be taken into account 
(Jon G. Gluyas, 2001).  
The average value for permeability in vertical direction and horizontal direction are 
4.41 𝑚𝑑 and 7.08 𝑚𝑑 respectively, these values for samples from Stvens chalk is reported 
as 3.58 𝑚𝑑 and 3.02 for vertical and horizontal direction correspondingly in Korsnes’s 
study (R. I. Korsnes, 2008). 
Kozeny’s equation represents permeability and porosity relationship. The values of 
permeability and porosity in this study could be checked by porosity-permeability plot 
which is obtained by Kozeny’s equation. 
The average of porosity for all the samples in this study is 44.7%, by using this porosity in 
equation 44, calculate Kozeny’s constant (𝑐). 𝑐 for sample with mentioned porosity 
is 0.243. The specific surface area for Stevns chalk in this study is assumed as 1.4 𝑚2/𝑔 and 
average grain densities for samples based on the measurement is 2.7 𝑔/𝑐𝑐 .Permeability 
can be calculated by using equation 43 for range of porosity from 0 to 100%. Figure 30 
represents porosity-permeability relation based on the Kozeny’s equation. In this plot the 
values of porosity and permeability for samples in this study are marked.  
Figure 30 confirms that samples with relatively close porosity are chosen. Selecting 
samples with close values of porosity to each other minimize effect of porosity on the 
strength of samples and other mechanical propperties. Calculation of permeability based 
on Kozeny’s equation is brought in Appendix 8.

4-3- Saturation 
In this study the selected samples are saturated and all the tests are carried out for 
saturated samples. Section 3-2-3 briefly explained the saturation procedure and in this 
section the result of the procedure and calculation is presented. 
For calculation of saturation first of all the density of mixed solution of distilled water and 
chalk powder is measured which was equal to0.9983 𝑔𝑐𝑚3
⁄
. The weight of dry sample and wet 
sample are also measured, subtract these two value in order to measure the mixed solution, 
which enters into the pore space of sample. The definition of density for solution was used and 
volume of solution that filled the pore space was calculated. Finally based on the definition of 
saturation, which is fraction of fluid in given pore volume, the saturation of sample could be 
calculated as follow. 
𝑚𝑠𝑎𝑡−𝑚𝑑𝑟𝑦= 𝑚𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛 
𝜌𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛= 𝑚𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛
𝑣𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛
→𝑣𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛= 𝑚𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛
𝜌𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛
 
𝑆𝑤= 𝑣𝑚𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑑 𝑠𝑜𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛
𝑉𝑝𝑜𝑟𝑒
 
64

completely filled by mixed solution. During the week samples were weighed three times in
